< Text>
Super kind staff. I enjoyed it all, but the Chana Masala was SO good! And thank you for the samosas. They were heavenly! What is that sweet, red sauce?! I will be a regular customer even if that's all I get. But their store has an amazing array of items. I got some very hard to find medicinal foods and items for a very reasonable amount. The price of their food and their store products are inexpensive. It's those hole-in-the-wall shops that surprise you the most. You made a new customer!< /Text>

<time>1545939563156</time><rating>5<//rating>< review>
If you are a Parata lover, this is a must visit place. This is basically a Grocery Sore with Restaurant. They also serve buffet. You must try their Paratas, with a chunk of butter on top of it. We tried, Aloo, Gobi, Muli and Methi Paratas, all were simply out of this world. Pickle and Boondi raita were also awesome. Service was reasonably quick, considering they make fresh parata after you order. If you are driving on Hwy 99 stop by at this place.</review>

<text>Tried Magic Kingdom and Sky Odyssey as a group of 3. Magic Kingdom was simple, whimsical, and fun, without being too short. Very kid-friendly.

Sky Odyssey was right up my alley, but not for everyone‚ÄîYou're exposed to a lot pretty early on, so you have to stay focused on what you actually need, what you can do, and what you've already done at any given point. It would have helped us to have 5 or more people in our group.

Our gamemaster Will was very experienced and enthusiastic. He gave us bonus time at the end of Sky Odyssey to solve the puzzles we didn't solve (84 minutes total), and he was still willing to answer all of our questions afterwards.

Other notes:
-The lobby looks a little run down, but the rooms are well decorated.
-Don't watch the lobby TV unless you're okay with some spoilers.

<review>We have been doing quite a lot of escape rooms over the past few months, so by this point I figured I had seen it all. Then Maze Escape rooms blew us away with Magic Kingdom, and I feel like I experience a new take on rooms that I highly recommend to both new players, and veterans alike. If you are experienced, don't expect a challenge, just enjoy the presentation and fact that you won't have to open a single lock, use a single key, or find any combinations. Every clue you solve is done through  the use of the "Magic" (aka technology) in the rooms. Definitely bring kids as its geared towards them more.

We also stuck around and did a second run on Secret Mission, as we were really happy with Magic Kingdom. While the theme and some puzzles were cool, overall it didn't feel quite as cohesive to us. We did bring a kid (who was there for Magic Kingdom but stuck around with us), and another person who was experience escape rooms for the first time, but the other 4 of us have done around 8 different rooms by now. This was the second time we ever came close to failing, with the last time being the first game we ever attempted. The biggest hurdle I think came from us discovering a clue earlier than we were supposed to, which caused us to trigger a really cool event at the same time as we were trying to solve that puzzle, leading us to think it was already resolved when in fact it wasn't. After the game, when it was explained to us, it all made sense logically, but in the moment it tripped us up and caused us to lose quite a bit of time. This was also one of the first games where a puzzle was solved by doing seemingly unrelated (but clearly related in hindsight) puzzles that had gated us from progressing in the puzzles. I don't think this is entirely the fault of the game, because as a whole the experience was totally positive, but we went from solving rooms with 10-20 minutes left to getting out with 2 minutes left!

That being said, we are super excited to come back and try Lunar Mission in the future, the staff was engaged and helpful and the fact you get to wear costume pieces to enhance the experience was very cool.<//review><pics>None< /pics><Response>None< /Response>< gmap_id>

<rate>5</rate><Text>LUNAR STATION is the one!

In short words:
The most impressive, innovative escape game in LA, with production value as good as Disneyland. This is a MUST TRY.

In long words:
If you think of first generation of escape game (locks and keys, paper hidden under the drawer) as parks near your home; most other escape games (some mechanic gadgets but still classic puzzles) as carnival; THE LUNER STATION is Hollywood studio!

We came here on the second day of opening. before game starts, we got our gears - astronauts' outfit, backpack and a black box to secure the tube. Then we split up into 2 teams. As we only have 2 players, one got stuck in the moon station and one came as rescue team.

There aren't any typical puzzles as in some other escape rooms that you can tell were separated from the theme. All the puzzles in Lunar Station make perfect sense, and more importantly, ALL fit the theme.

We were constantly surprised during this interactive journey by its game design, decoration, lighting and sounding effect, let alone the most awesome ending. From all the details, you can tell how much time and effort they put into this game. Thank you Maze Game, for bringing us such a great game.

We were told a new fairy theme one is under construction, and it will be even better than Lunar Station. We can't wait to come back!<//Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures><Resp>None<//Resp>< GmapID>

Update: Still no answer from messaging them, good luck to anybody trying to contact.  Changing to one star from two.

The first time I ate here was good.  Everything was correct and the food was good.  This time around my order was wrong and I didn't realize it until later.  I have a bad habit of trusting places to not make mistakes but this wasn't even a minor mistake.  I ordered a portobello mushroom charburger with sourdough substitute and added bacon. < Review>
First time to eat at The Habit today. A friend recommended it to me because he knows I love cheese burgers. The first thing I noticed when we walked in was the temperature in the restaurant, warm. If the A/C was on it was set pretty high. Very stuffy stagnate air in the dinning area. Was greated by a friendly women who I assumed was a manager or shift leader because she was wearing a different colored shirt than everyone else. I ordered the sesonal item, Santa Barbara Char burger. Comes with 2 burger patties both topped with cheddar cheese and grilled onions, lettuce, tomatoes, pickles and avocado. I also got an order of fries, well done,  because lets be honest, fries are never as crispy as they should be because restaurants are in such a hurry to get food out. Also ordered the tempura green beans. My friend got the single char with swiss, grilled onions and lettuce. He's kind of a plain guy, I always say you can tell a lot about a person by how they order a cheese burger. Anywho my Santa Barbara burger was good the patties were seasoned properly the cheese was perfectly gooey, melty, the grilled onions were ok. Not as carmelized as they could be in my opinion. The Santa Barbara char comes on grilled bread not your traditional hamburger bun. All in all a pretty good burger. It just still has that synthetic fast food feel about it. No home made love feel like I get at In n Out or Riders Club. The fries were cooked well as I ordered them but you could tell they were frozen. Definitely not In n Out fresh cut quality. The tempura green beans were good. But for $2.99 I feel like we should have got more than what they gave us, kinda stingy if you know what I mean. Drink selection was good. I'm an iced tea guy so it was pretty cool they had three fresh brewed teas to choose from, black tea, tropical tea and a citrus green tea. Also had strawberry limeade which was pretty good. In the end I would eat here again if I was in the area and didn't want to wait the 15 minutes it would take to get to In n Out.< /Review>

<UserId.>109128655814929790511</UserId.>< review>
First time to eat at The Habit today. A friend recommended it to me because he knows I love cheese burgers. The first thing I noticed when we walked in was the temperature in the restaurant, warm. If the A/C was on it was set pretty high. Very stuffy stagnate air in the dinning area. Was greated by a friendly women who I assumed was a manager or shift leader because she was wearing a different colored shirt than everyone else. I ordered the sesonal item, Santa Barbara Char burger. Comes with 2 burger patties both topped with cheddar cheese and grilled onions, lettuce, tomatoes, pickles and avocado. I also got an order of fries, well done,  because lets be honest, fries are never as crispy as they should be because restaurants are in such a hurry to get food out. Also ordered the tempura green beans. My friend got the single char with swiss, grilled onions and lettuce. He's kind of a plain guy, I always say you can tell a lot about a person by how they order a cheese burger. Anywho my Santa Barbara burger was good the patties were seasoned properly the cheese was perfectly gooey, melty, the grilled onions were ok. Not as carmelized as they could be in my opinion. The Santa Barbara char comes on grilled bread not your traditional hamburger bun. All in all a pretty good burger. It just still has that synthetic fast food feel about it. No home made love feel like I get at In n Out or Riders Club. The fries were cooked well as I ordered them but you could tell they were frozen. Definitely not In n Out fresh cut quality. The tempura green beans were good. But for $2.99 I feel like we should have got more than what they gave us, kinda stingy if you know what I mean. Drink selection was good. I'm an iced tea guy so it was pretty cool they had three fresh brewed teas to choose from, black tea, tropical tea and a citrus green tea. Also had strawberry limeade which was pretty good. In the end I would eat here again if I was in the area and didn't want to wait the 15 minutes it would take to get to In n Out.<//review>
